### Post by paarthri on 2015-10-21
Hello community.
I am new to dual booting and do not want to mess up my computer because it is my main machine. It would be great if I could have some detailed instructions on how to dual boot Ubuntu LTS with Windows 10. I know this sounds greedy or selfish, but I can not find instructions for my model specifically.

Here are my specs:
Intel core i7 processor
8 gigs of ram
no dedicated gpu

I will gladly clear up anything else needed. 

Thanks in advance,
Paarth Tandon

### Post by oldfred on 2015-10-22
This is one thread with your exact model.
 Lenovo Z510 Laptop & Ubuntu 
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2232124](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2232124)

General UEFI install info:
      
 Shows install with screen shots. Both BIOS purple accessibility screen & UEFI black grub menu screen
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UEFI](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UEFI)
Also shows Windows 8 screeens
[http://askubuntu.com/questions/221835/installing-ubuntu-on-a-pre-installed-uefi-supported-windows-8-system](http://askubuntu.com/questions/221835/installing-ubuntu-on-a-pre-installed-uefi-supported-windows-8-system)
UEFI install,windows 8 with Something Else screen shots
[http://www.everydaylinuxuser.com/2014/05/install-ubuntu-1404-alongside-windows.html](http://www.everydaylinuxuser.com/2014/05/install-ubuntu-1404-alongside-windows.html)
Linux on UEFI: A Quick Installation Guide
[http://www.rodsbooks.com/linux-uefi/](http://www.rodsbooks.com/linux-uefi/)
Something Else or manual Install
[http://www.dedoimedo.com/computers/dual-boot-windows-8-ubuntu.html](http://www.dedoimedo.com/computers/dual-boot-windows-8-ubuntu.html)

Also link below in my signature has many useful links & details

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]### BEGIN /etc/grub.d/00_header ###[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ -s $prefix/grubenv ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ "${next_entry}" ] ; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   set default="${next_entry}"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   set next_entry=[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   save_env next_entry[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   set boot_once=true[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   set default="0"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ x"${feature_menuentry_id}" = xy ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  menuentry_id_option="--id"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  menuentry_id_option=""[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]export menuentry_id_option[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ "${prev_saved_entry}" ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set saved_entry="${prev_saved_entry}"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  save_env saved_entry[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set prev_saved_entry=[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  save_env prev_saved_entry[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set boot_once=true[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]function savedefault {[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  if [ -z "${boot_once}" ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    saved_entry="${chosen}"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    save_env saved_entry[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  fi[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]}[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]function recordfail {[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set recordfail=1[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  if [ -n "${have_grubenv}" ]; then if [ -z "${boot_once}" ]; then save_env recordfail; fi; fi[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]}[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]function load_video {[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  if [ x$feature_all_video_module = xy ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod all_video[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod efi_gop[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod efi_uga[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod vbe[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod vga[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod video_bochs[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    insmod video_cirrus[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  fi[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]}[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ x$feature_default_font_path = xy ] ; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]   font=unicode[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]insmod part_gpt[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]insmod ext2[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]set root='hd0,gpt10'[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ x$feature_platform_search_hint = xy ]; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  search --no-floppy --fs-uuid --set=root --hint-bios=hd0,gpt10 --hint-efi=hd0,gpt10 --hint-baremetal=ahci0,gpt10  9611f06f-fb31-47f3-830f-623e8fe47435[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  search --no-floppy --fs-uuid --set=root 9611f06f-fb31-47f3-830f-623e8fe47435[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    font="/usr/share/grub/unicode.pf2"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if loadfont $font ; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set gfxmode=auto[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  insmod gfxterm[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  insmod gettext[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]if [ "${recordfail}" = 1 ] ; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  set timeout=10[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  if [ x$feature_timeout_style = xy ] ; then[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    set timeout_style=menu[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    set timeout=10[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  # Fallback normal timeout code in case the timeout_style feature is[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  # unavailable.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  else[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]    set timeout=10[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]  fi[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]fi[/FONT][/COLOR]

### Post by oldfred on 2015-10-30
This causes issues for Ubuntu. But not directly booting Windows from UEFI boot menu.

>  The disk contains an unclean file system (0, 0).
Metadata kept in Windows cache, refused to mount.
Failed to mount '/dev/sda5': Operation not permitted
The NTFS partition is in an unsafe state. Please resume and shutdown
Windows fully (no hibernation or fast restarting), or mount the volume
read-only with the 'ro' mount option.
mount -t ntfs-3g -o remove_hiberfile /dev/sda5 /mnt/boot-sav/sda5



       Fast Startup off/hibernation - Windows 8 or 10 UEFI or BIOS boot.
[http://www.eightforums.com/tutorials/6320-fast-startup-turn-off-windows-8-a.html](http://www.eightforums.com/tutorials/6320-fast-startup-turn-off-windows-8-a.html)
[http://www.kapilarya.com/how-to-enable-disable-fast-start-up-in-windows-8](http://www.kapilarya.com/how-to-enable-disable-fast-start-up-in-windows-8)

### Post by ubfan1 on 2015-10-30
I assume your errors are /EFI/... instead of UEFI/... That would be a problem if not the case.
I see the EFI partition mount in /etc/fstab is commented out (the #) -- not sure if that's causing any problems, but mine looks like:
# /boot/efi was on /dev/sda2 during installation
UUID=7A11-7B8B                            /boot/efi       vfat    defaults        0       1
Yours is:[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]
#UUID=0C86-5E58  /boot/efi       vfat    umask=0077      0       1

Another item is in the /EFI/Boot directory, you have a bkpbootx64.efi (I assume this is the Windows bootloader boot-repair renamed, check the size to confirm) and /EFI/bootx64.efi which is a default bootloader, either a renamed copy of shimx64.efi or grubx64.efi (check the sizes).  Now if it's grubx64.efi, that wont work with secure boot on.  If it's shimx64.efi, you are missing a copy of grubx64.efi in the same directory.  It's good to have a working setup here, it may actually get used. I like to use shimx64.efi as bootx64.efi since that works with or without secure boot.
  Now sda3 looks like a backup EFI partition, but it's missing grubx74.efi in the /EFI/ubuntu directory (and maybe others).  I'd make those file match the ones in sda2, which is the boot-flagged EFI partition.  

[/FONT][/COLOR]

### Post by oldfred on 2015-10-31
Were you manually booting the copies in sda3.
Lenovo creates another hidden FAT32 partition for its own boot files which I assume are for system functions or recovery. It may then change boot flag or othewise allow its use for booting. Yours is sda2, but it looks like Ubuntu installed or Boot-Repair copied boot files into it also which it probably should not have done.

New versions of Ubuntu have changed the mount of the ESP from defaults to umask=0077 which is a bummer. From inside your install you cannot modify you own ESP files. You have to boot a live installer. Or change fstab setting back to defaults. And changing to defaults and reloading fstab does not work, you have to reboot.

Some Lenovo have a locked boot order, or other UEFI settings that must be changed:

       T540 works but UEFI settings critical or it may brick
[https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hFTArhNbmpmEBRkwRg0DMbEzLBCl43F1HXoXtJ8cm0k/edit?pli=1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hFTArhNbmpmEBRkwRg0DMbEzLBCl43F1HXoXtJ8cm0k/edit?pli=1)
Lenovo Thinkpad E531 - turn off locked boot order setting in UEFI
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2255746](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2255746)
[SOLVED] Error 1962: No operating system found. Lenovo K430  only boot Ubuntu, rename files
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2243715](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2243715)

    
And some systems just will not boot ubuntu UEFI entry and we have to copy shim into /EFI/Boot and rename to bootx64.efi. Then boot a hard drive entry or fallback entry in UEFI. You may have to create that entry also. Back up ESP - efi system partition first.
       [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2234019](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2234019)

Even more details on renaming to bootx64.efi in link in my signature.
